text:
Great basic recipe, but I needed to adjust it.  A 16 oz. pkg of noodles is too much. The recipe needs more seasoning and less creamy stuff.  Here's what I changed:  8 oz. of med. egg noodles; 1.5 lbs. lean gr. beef - brown the gr. beef and add in the gravy mix plus 3 Tbsp Worcestershire sauce, fresh ground black pepper to taste and 1 cup of minced yellow onion. Cook that for a couple of minutes and then add 4 oz. (instead of 8 oz) of cream cheese and stir on low heat until incorporated.  Then follow the directions exactly except use 1.5 cans of the cr of mushroom soup.  Hopes this helps others. I like the way that this recipe mixes the ingredients together. Thanks!

text:
The first time I made this (as written) it was way too thick and creamy for my tastes. However, I love this recipe as a base. I agree with some other reviewers that it has too many artificial flavors. The way I like it is with homemade cream of mushroom soup from this site, (though I will use the canned stuff in a pinch) 3 or 4 oz. of cream cheese, maybe 6 or so oz. sour cream (I'm not much for measuring) and I don't usually have brown gravy mix so I use beef soup base and spices. I always use fresh garlic, onions and mushrooms, and more milk to make it the right consistency.

text:
I used a can of beef gravy instead of the dry mix, and added chopped sauteed onions and minced garlic.  Because most of the reviewers complained it had too much sour cream & cream cheese, I used 2 TB of each, tasted, and added slightly more sour cream as needed.  I also only used 1 can of cream of mushroom soup.  I used low fat cream cheese & sour cream and you wouldn't know the difference.  I also added some worchestshire sauce to taste. I had some leftover flank steak and chopped that up and put in there too. Served over egg noodles.  Hubby went back for seconds and the kids even enjoyed.  I'll be having what little is left for lunch.  Real comfort food for sure.  I will make again.

text:
This was excellent. So quick and easy to make, and then so tasty! As other reviewers suggested, I used only half the cream cheese called for (actually I used neufchatel cheese in order to cut back on fat a bit), and I used fresh sliced mushrooms instead of canned. I sauteed the mushrooms and some diced onions together, then browned the meat (I used ground turkey) with them. I added seasoned salt for a little more flavor. I used low fat sour cream and the 98% fat free cream of mushroom soup. And it was delicious! My boyfriend took the first bite and simply raved. Then later he went back for a huge helping of seconds. I will be making this again. A quick and easy, delicious dinner that only used two pots - a great find!

My family said it was totally delish. I ended up making a double batch, but as I got into the recipe, I totally forgot got to make sure I had double the amount of noodles. Soo I ended up making it as planned and saved half the batch of meat mixture for the next day's lunch. Now I followed the rest of the recipe to a T and have never used cream cheese in stroganoff before and I can say, it really added texture and creaminess. At 1st I really thought it was too saucy but after I used the batch over the noodles, it was fine. Over night of course it thickened and when I reheated the 2nd batch with another bit of noodles I had to add milk to thin it out some, it was fine. Will make again. Thanks

text:
This was a real throw-back to my childhood, and a great way to use up extra ground beef after a bbq and some leftover noodles from something else!  Not a gourmet experience, but tasty comfort food that is easily adaptable to your tastes or what items you have on hand.  Like nearly everyone else, I also only used about half the (light) cream cheese called for, and probably only 6 oz of Low Fat sour cream.  Didn't have milk so I used FF half-n-half and water combo.  I did use both cans of cream soups, which really was more than necessary--but I didn't want to throw any out, either. I totally forgot to add the gravy mix, so I just sprinkled some TexMex Chipotle Spices into the skillet for more flavor.  Omitted the mushrooms (I would have used fresh ones if I had any) and added frozen peas, as another reviewed suggested, which was a good addition. Salt & peppered it liberally. Love one-skillet meals, and this is a good base recipe that I am sure I will come back to again in the future.

text:
Very tasty, filling, rich. 
I saut√©ed one white onion, a tablespoon of jarred chopped garlic, 1 teaspoon each: salt, fresh ground pepper, onion powder; 2 tablespoons of Worcestershire sauce along with the ground beef for extra depth of flavor and would recommend that you try it too. I suspect it might have been somewhat bland without the extra seasonings. I used a container of fresh sliced white button mushrooms instead of canned, since I had fresh ones on hand.

I'll definitely try making this again in the future, but will try to lighten up the sauce a bit. Perhaps will try using light sour cream, low fat milk, reduced fat mushroom soup, and light cream cheese. We loved the flavor & comforting aspect of this hearty, easy meal. Quick to assemble & cook it, and light years better quality than similar hamburger type boxed dinners.

Served it over egg noodles, with green salads, fresh corn, warm French bread alongside. I'd like to try it over brown rice next time instead. Thanks for the great recipe!

Very good! I did change a few things. We don't like cream of mushroom so I used cream of onion instead. Only used 1 can didn't use the mushrooms either. Used about 1cup of milk, used about 3/4 of the cream cheese and used a 2.75oz pack of dry brown gravy mix. I did have to add a good bit of salt afterwards for extra flavor. Next time I will season my meat mixture a good bit while cooking it. And make sure the cream cheese is softened I actually had to melt mine with the hamburger meat. Mine turned out much thicker than the picture because I didn't use as much of the liquids called for, but this was a VERY good recipe that I WILL make again. My husband and kids even liked it and they are VERY picky eaters.

Delicious! Per other suggestions, I decreased the amount of cream cheese & sour cream to 1/2 of what was called for, & used 1&1/2 cans of the mushroom soup.  In a lot of recipes involving pasta, I like to reduce the amount called for, but I ended up going back and making all 16oz of pasta because there's a lot of sauce.  **I would highly recommend adding black pepper, garlic powder (about 1&1/2 tsp, depending on taste), & onion, plus a dash or two of parsley & oregano for a more flavorful aftertaste, & a bit of color. This is plenty for 2 people to have 2-3 meals.

text:
After reading a few of the other reviews I went ahead and did my own thing. I had just under a lb of ground beef and I found in my freezer about a 1/2 lb of mild Italian sausage so I defrosted that and added to the ground beef. Drained that. Added a small yellow onion, chopped and 2 cloves of minced garlic. Added some Worcestershire, maybe 2 tbsps. Salt & ground pepper. Let that simmer for about 10 min. Then added one can of beef broth and one can of cream of mushroom soup. Then a small can of drained mushroom pieces. (should've added anther can). Let that cook for about 15-20 min. Just before serving, I added about 1/2 sour cream and blended it into the meat mixture. Poured over wide egg noodles.

BUT... a MAJOR component of EVERY good Stroganoff recipe I've ever seen, made or eaten includes wine, usually SHERRY! It serves as a counterbalance to cut the excessive richness & thickness I've read so many complaints about here.

I'll check back after I make it... with SHERRY!!!

This stroganoff was fantastic!
I made some slight modifications....

* I used 8-10 sliced fresh mushrooms (Instead of using the canned mushrooms).  When the ground beef was almost browned I added them to the meat & onions, covering the skillet until mushrooms were almost done.

* Add fresh ground salt and ground pepper to taste.

text:
I give it a 5 because it was a great base to start with.  And it seemed pretty simple so I was encouraged to try it when I didn't have a ton of time to fix dinner.  I did read reviews before and made changes to my tastes.  While cooking the 16 oz bag of egg noodles, I browned 1.5 lbs hamburger, small minced onion and
 2 cloves minced garlic all together in deep pan and drained.  Then added to pan 1 T Better than Beef Bouillon instead of the gravy packet, 1/2 c. water because I left the mushrooms out. 4 oz. cream cheese, 1 t seasoned salt, 2 cans cream of mushroom soup, 8 oz sour cream,  1 c. milk to  thin a little more, 1/4 c. cooking sherry because I didn't have red wine, 1 small bag baby frozen green peas (I needed a complete meal to serve to my aging parents in their 90's) Add additional salt and pepper to taste.  This makes a large portion, but it was all gone in a few days.  I'll make it again and invite guest over.  All of my changes were pretty much suggested by another reviewer at some point.  I just adjusted to the most common suggestions and a few that I thought would be good ideas for our tastes.  With adding the peas and you have a one dish meal.

text:
I made this with all the listed (forgot the dang mushrooms at the store though...) ingredients with a few tweaks. IT WAS AMAZING! My Wife and I both loved it (she's the picky eater btw ;). It was dinner and didn't make it past lunch today.
First part : I pre cooked the burger with a touch of ground pepper, dash of Worcestershire and granulated garlic. Cooked the Amish egg noodles in a light amount of beef stock (Better than Bouillon brand)  in the water (yes you can do that!) strained and set aside.
Second part: I did this a hour or so later, used half of the cream cheese, cream mushroom soup and subbed the sour cream with 2% plain good for you Greek yogurt (careful, greek yogurt is not good at high heat due to low fat content) and 2% lowfat milk. Cooked on low and slowly added the milk till I got the consistency I liked. Added the noodles and beef and simmered for 5 minutes stirring slowly. It was the perfect amount to cover and infuse the beef and noodles with flavor. I think it would NOT have been good using the full amount of cream cheese etc in my stupid opinion.
 Next I plan on making this swapping out the noodles for sliced potatoes. I shall call this dish Mike's Beef Potatoganoff! I'll post that if you guys want.

region:

country:

text:
If you are looking for an easy, tasty beef stroganoff recipe this is it!  I have a few things to say, so bear with me!  Based on the few reviews I read, I changed things slightly and it turned out great!
I only used 4 oz cream cheese.  Also, I used low fat sour cream.  I also used about 1 1/2 lbs of ground beef because that is how much was in the package I had.  I'm glad I used the extra beef.  Otherwise I think there may have been too much sauce to meat ratio.  The following is very important-- I seasoned the beef with salt, pepper, garlic powder, minced onions, thyme and marjoram while cooking.  I think this recipe would have been too bland otherwise.
Also, the step that says to mix the mushroom soup, milk and sour cream to noodles you do not have to do it that way.  I mixed those ingredients in a bowl, then stirred it into the pan containing the beef mixture.  I did this because my husband likes regular egg noodles and I use wheat egg noodles.  By mixing it this way we could spoon the stroganoff sauce onto our noodles to taste.  
This stroganoff is very rich and delicious.  Easy for a week night dinner.

text:
I cut the cream cheese by half, used one can of golden mushroom soup and one can of cream of mushroom, and two four ounce cans of sliced mushrooms.  Other than that, the only thing I did differently was the steps since they didn't make sense to me.

I browned the ground beef and drained it, then added the brown gravy powder, milk, soups, mushrooms, and cream cheese.  I cooked that on medium low until the cream cheese was melted and the whole thing was bubbly.  I cooked the noodles in the meantime.  After I added the meat mixture to the noodles, I stirred in the sour cream.

I think next time I might try adding a splash of wine to give it a little lift.

text:
Quick, weeknight meal.  I used 1.5 lbs of beef and a used a full 1.2 oz Knorr brown gravy packet, but reduced cream cheese to 6 oz and sour cream to 4 oz per others suggestions.  I flavored the meat with garlic powder and a pinch of salt.  The meat mixture was really good prior to mixing with the mushroom soup.  Then I think it lost some of its flavor and became more processed tasting.  This is a decent quick dinner but I might need to tweak the soup mixture portion next time.  BTW, the color of this meal was a light gray when prepared (yuck).  I suppose if I added all the cream cheese and sour cream it may have looked more creamy in color.

text:
okay, so here's what i did:
when i browned the beef (a little over 1 lb.), i included a few cloves of minced garlic and about half a sweet onion, minced and salt & pepper to taste. once browned, i mixed in 2 tbsp. worcestershire sauce, a 1.25 oz. packet of mushroom & herb gravy (that's what i had on hand) and can of 'shrooms with liquid. then i mixed in 4 oz. of cream cheese until completely combined.
then i mixed a can and a half of the cream of 'shroom soup and a cup of milk. while it simmered, i cooked the whole 16 oz. package of egg noodles. to serve, we topped the noodles with the burger sauce by the plate and then added our own individual amount of sour cream. this was so awesome!!! it made for great leftovers, too!

Delicious! I did make some changes (sorry all those that hate recipe alterations)... I didn't have enough sour cream, so I used 4 ounces sour cream and 4 ounces cottage cheese. I didn't use canned mushrooms, but used 8 ounces fresh, sliced mushrooms. In place of the mushroom juice from the can, I used heavy cream. I used a Beef Gravy with Herbs gravy mix. I only had one can of cream of mushroom soup (low fat), so I also used a can of cream of celery soup. Mine turned out deliciously! So creamy and flavorful! Thank you for the diving board!

I made a few changes to this recipe based on other people's reviews and it turned out really well.  I halved the sour cream and soup, and it still turned out really creamy.  I also used fresh mushrooms instead of canned.  Minced garlic, salt and pepper also really helped with the flavouring.  Will make it again.

text:
I followed the recipe pretty closely; I mixed all the ingredients into the skillet with the beef, instead of combining the sourcream and soup with the pasta first. I also omitted one can of soup. I used brown gravy mix out of a large container, instead of an individual packet (probably about 2 Tbs). I think that this was very easy and fairly tasty... there was something about the flavor I really wasn't thrilled with. I think it was the hamburger honestly, I think this would have tasted better to me with a cut of steak instead of hamburger. I might make it again, but I think I would use something other than hamburger next time, I would also half the cream cheese!
